KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, BLOCK
46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM
PROVISION OF EPCI
KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan
1 INTRODUCTION
PVEP–KHANH MY (herein referred to as COMPANY) is undertaking development of Khanh
My and Dam Doi fields, which are located in Block 46/13, Malay - Tho Chu Basin, S. R.
Vietnam, approximately 205 km southwest of Cape Ca Mau and about 30 km northwest of the
Bunga Kekwa field of Block PM3 CAA, with a water depth of approximately 53 m. The
Project First Gas is expected in Quarter 4 of 2027.
Location map of Block 46/13 is as shown in Figure 1.
Figure 1 Location map of Block 46/13
The development of Khanh My and Dam Doi fields will comprise of the following new
facilities:
- One (1) unmanned wellhead platform KM-WHP.
- One (1) unmanned wellhead platform DD-WHP.
- 20” x 6.7 km long FWS rigid pipeline from KM-WHP to DD-WHP.
- 20” x 22.0 km long FWS rigid pipeline from DD-WHP to the existing BK-C WHRP.
- Subsea pig-gable wye fitting which has one inlet spared for Block 46-CN Development
located at tie-in point approximately 14 km downstream of DD-WHP.
Document No.: KDP-000-03-PS-G-0001-A0
Page No.: 8 of 57

KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, BLOCK
46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM
PROVISION OF EPCI
KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan
Development scheme of Khanh My and Dam Doi fields is as shown in Figure 2.
Figure 2 Field development scheme
In addition, the field development will also consist of modifications to the existing BK- C
WHRP and BR-A CPP of Block PM3 CAA including:
- A new retrofit 20” riser and clamps, structural deck extension, topside piping and
valves, pig receiver, allocation gas metering skid, electrical terminations, and
associated miscellaneous work on BK-C WHRP.
- Upgrade of the existing DCS on BR-A CPP for operation monitoring and remote
control of KM-WHP and DD-WHP.
- Upgrade of the existing Telecom, Network System on BR-A CPP and HML’s office to
accommodate the KM-WHP, DD-WHP communication via Digital Microwave Radio
(DMR) to support operation monitoring and remote control; and data transmission from
HML’s office to PVEP-KHANH MY’s office.
Produced fluids of Khanh My and Dam Doi fields will be transferred from KM-WHP and DD-
WHP to BK-C WHRP, and then to the existing processing facilities at PM3 Southern Field
(PM3S) prior to exporting from Bunga Raya-B platform (BR-B WHRP) to Vietnam shore via
the existing 18” PM3 - Ca Mau gas export pipeline. Separated condensates will be stored in
and offloaded later from FSO PM-3 CAA.
Document No.: KDP-000-03-PS-G-0001-A0
Page No.: 9 of 57

KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan

|     |     |     |     |     |     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

The platforms will be remotely monitored and controlled from BR-A CPP of Block PM3 CAA
as well as being monitored from mainland of Vietnam. Dedicated facilities of PM3S will be
modified, upgraded or extended to cater for additional production and additional facilities to
be monitored and controlled.
KM-WHP and DD-WHP are designed as unmanned platforms for burn down concepts and
minimum facilities. Each new platform has a total of four (04) conductor slots, and each
conductor slot is designed to accommodate two (02) individual wells. The facilities are
designed for simultaneous drilling and production (SIPROD).
The topsides facilities and subsea pipelines will have a design life of 10 years. The platform
structures will have a design life of 15 years.

PROVISION OF EPCI
KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan
Risk Management Plan
1.4 PURPOSE AND OBJECTIVE
The purpose of this Engineering Execution Plan (EEP) is to define the overall engineering
execution philosophy, management approach, control measures, work processes, and
coordination arrangements to be adopted for the Project.
This EEP is prepared to establish a unified framework for the planning, execution,
coordination, monitoring, control, and delivery of the full engineering scope of the Project,
covering greenfield facilities, including KM & DD WHP Topsides, Jackets and Pipeline, as
well as the brownfield modification scope. Ensuring that all engineering activities performed
by CONTRACTOR and its engineering subcontractors are executed in a structured, integrated,
timely, and controlled manner, in line with contractual requirements, project priorities,
applicable codes and standards, and the overall project execution strategy.
The objectives of this Engineering Execution Plan are to:
- Establish a clear and integrated engineering execution framework for the full Project
scope under CONTRACTOR’s overall responsibility.
- Define the engineering execution strategy, organization, responsibilities, interfaces,
reporting lines, and control principles applicable to CONTRACTOR and all
engineering subcontractors involved in the Project.
- Ensure that the engineering work for Topsides, Jackets, Pipeline, and Brownfield scope
is planned, coordinated, and executed in a consistent manner and aligned with the
overall Project schedule, procurement priorities, construction sequence, installation
strategy, and commissioning requirements.
- Define the engineering management systems, procedures, workflows, and control
measures required for effective execution and integration of multidisciplinary
engineering activities across all work packages.
- Ensure that engineering deliverables are developed and issued in accordance with the
required design maturity, applicable review and approval workflow, and the needs of
downstream procurement, fabrication, construction, installation, hook-up,
commissioning, and follow-on engineering activities.
- Establish a robust framework for management of engineering inputs, design basis,
technical assumptions, interfaces, technical clarifications, vendor data, comments,
revisions, and engineering changes throughout the engineering lifecycle.

1.5 OVERALL SCOPE OF ENGINEERING WORK
The Project engineering scope covers the engineering activities required for the development,
coordination, integration, review, and delivery of the Project facilities, including both
greenfield and brownfield scope, under the overall responsibility of Vietsovpetro (VSP) as the
EPCI CONTRACTOR.
VSP, as the EPCI CONTRACTOR, is responsible for overall project coordination and
integration. Each engineering subcontractor bears full technical and quality responsibility for
deliverables within its own assigned scope.
For execution purposes, the engineering scope is allocated to the following parties:
PTSC M&C is assigned as the EPC subcontractor for the KM & DD WHP Topsides scope,
including the related multidisciplinary engineering activities such as Process, Mechanical,
HVAC, Piping and Layout, Instrumentation, Telecommunications, Electrical, Topsides
Structural, Technical Safety, 3D Model development, and relevant follow-on engineering
support.
NIPI is assigned as the engineering subcontractor for the KM & DD WHP Jackets and Subsea
Pipeline scope, including Jacket structural engineering, Pipeline engineering, and other related
engineering activities required for the assigned package, together with the relevant interface
coordination and follow-on engineering support.
For Brownfield Modification: [HOLD 1 – To be updated upon nomination of Brownfield
Engineering Subcontractor]. The Brownfield scope is expected to include site surveys,
modification engineering, and related follow-on engineering support.

2 PROJECT ENGINEERING EXECUTION STRATEGY
2.1 EXECUTION PHILOSOPHY
The Project shall be executed on a fast-track basis under tight schedule and budget constraints.
Accordingly, the engineering philosophy shall be to deliver a design that is fit for purpose,
practical, while fully supporting timely procurement, fabrication, installation, and
commissioning. Unnecessary design complication, over-design, and excessive conservatism
shall be avoided.
As a governing principle, the established FEED philosophy shall be maintained and developed
further in a reasonably practical and controlled manner. The objective is to preserve design
continuity, minimize rework, and protect the overall execution sequence. Engineering shall be
managed to achieve early definition and timely freeze of key design inputs, package
requirements, design basis, and interfaces so that procurement can proceed at the earliest
practical stage. Deliverables shall therefore be developed progressively in line with the
required design maturity and downstream Project needs. Once aligned, changes shall be
minimized and strictly controlled, particularly where they may affect cost, schedule,
procurement, fabrication, installation, or brownfield integration.
For this Project, Schedule and Topsides weight are the two dominant engineering drivers. All
major engineering decisions shall therefore be assessed against their impact on both. Weight
control is particularly critical, as the offshore lifting capacity of the designated Heavy Lifting
Vessel is limited to approximately 1000 MT as per FEED, while the current KM and DD WHP
Topsides design is already close to this threshold. Accordingly, all disciplines shall actively
control weight growth through practical design development, material selection, equipment
arrangement, and structural optimization, without compromising safety, functional
performance.
2.2 ADOPTED PRINCIPLES
The following principles set out below which are critical features for the execution of the
Detailed Engineering work to ensure proper control and coordination:
- Safety: Prioritize the safety of personnel, the operation, and the environment
throughout all phases of the project. Adhere to relevant safety regulations and
standards.
- Compliance: Ensure compliance with all relevant laws, regulations, codes, and
standards governing the project's scope and location.
Document No.: KDP-000-03-PS-G-0001-A0
Page No.: 17 of 57

KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, BLOCK
46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM
PROVISION OF EPCI
KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan
- Quality Assurance and Control: Implement rigorous quality assurance and quality
control measures to ensure that all project engineering activities meet or exceed
specified standards and requirements.
- Transparency and Communication: Foster open communication and transparency
among project stakeholders, including COMPANY, team members, Vendor, Sub-
contractors, and regulatory bodies.
- Change & Risk Management: Identify, assess, and mitigate project change and risks
proactively to prevent or strictly minimize potential project disruptions and delays. All
key engineering decisions shall be evaluated with due consideration to their impact on
overall Project schedule and Topsides weight.
- Collaboration and Teamwork: Promote collaboration and teamwork among all
project stakeholders to foster a cohesive and coordinated approach to project execution.
2.3 KEY SUCCESS FACTORS
The following key success factors are considered critical to enable all associated parties to
execute and complete the Detailed Engineering scope within the agreed schedule, cost, and
technical requirements:
- Strong overall engineering leadership and integration across all engineering parties and
work packages.
- Deployment of qualified and experienced personnel with strong execution mindset and
relevant project experience.
- Engineering priorities fully aligned with Procurement, Fabrication, Construction,
Installation, and Commissioning needs, especially for long lead and critical packages.
- Early definition and timely freeze of key design basis, critical inputs, and package
requirements to enable procurement at the earliest practical stage e.g. Flow Assurance,
P&ID, Layout, Basis of Design, Specifications, Philosophies, etc.
- Timely issuance of engineering deliverables with the required quality and design
maturity.
- Fast turnaround of review comments and approvals from COMPANY and other
involved parties, particularly for procurement-critical documents such as TR, TBE, and
key design deliverables.
- Effective interface management and disciplined coordination among Topsides, Jacket,
Pipeline, Brownfield, vendors, and all Project stakeholders.
- Strict control of Topsides weight growth throughout the design development,
recognizing weight as a major Project risk due to offshore lifting limitations.
- Early and practical constructability, operability, maintainability, and safety reviews to
ensure fit-for-purpose design and avoid late rework.

3 ENGINEERING MANAGEMENT AND CONTROL PLAN
3.1 ENGINEERING MANAGEMENT PLAN
The Project engineering work shall be executed through an integrated engineering framework
in which VSP, as the EPCI CONTRACTOR, provides overall project-level coordination,
planning oversight, and integration management. Each engineering party shall be individually
responsible and accountable for the execution quality, technical content, and schedule
performance of engineering within their respectively assigned scope.
VSP's engineering management role shall focus on ensuring alignment, coordination, and
timely information flow across packages. The day-to-day execution, technical decisions, and
delivery of engineering outputs within each package shall remain the direct responsibility of
the respective engineering subcontractor: PTSC M&C for the KM & DD WHP Topsides, NIPI
for the KM & DD WHP Jackets and Pipeline, and the future Brownfield subcontractor for the
Brownfield Modification scope.
Engineering management shall be implemented through a controlled system covering:
- Engineering planning (EMDR, Project Planning Tracker)
- Scope & Deliverables (Approved scope split, deliverables register)
- Progress measurement & Control (Discipline progress trackers, Dashboard, Progress
Report)
- Interdisciplinary coordination (IDC workflows, discipline coordination meetings,
model review sessions, and action tracking registers).
- Interface management (interface registers, IDR, interface meeting)
- Technical review & quality control (Self-check, SDC, IDC, design review checklists,
comment sheets)
- Document control (Procedure, DCC, Transmittal system)
- Vendor data control & incorporation (VDRL, Checklist, Expediting meeting)
- Technical change control (Procedure, DCN, TQR)
- Follow-on engineering support.
3.2 ENGINEERING OFFICE LOCATIONS AND WORKSHARE ARRANGEMENT
The Project engineering activities shall be executed through a multi-office arrangement within
Ho Chi Minh City, under the overall engineering leadership and integration control of
Vietsovpetro (VSP). Although the engineering work will be performed from different office
locations, all parties shall operate under one common engineering execution framework in

3.4 ROLES, RESPONSIBILITIES AND AUTHORITY
3.4.1 CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager (VSP)
The CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager is responsible for governing and managing all
engineering subcontractors on behalf of VSP throughout the Project lifecycle.
The main responsibilities of the CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager are:
- Manage and monitor the engineering performance of subcontractors against their
contracted scope, schedule, and quality obligations.
- Chair weekly engineering coordination meetings and ensure all action items are
assigned to the responsible subcontractor and tracked to closure.
- Review and authorize Design Change Notifications (DCN) and Technical Queries (TQ)
raised by subcontractors before submission to COMPANY.
- Report engineering execution status, subcontractor performance, and key risks to the
CONTRACTOR Project Manager.
3.4.2 CONTRACTOR Lead Discipline Engineer (VSP)
The CONTRACTOR Lead Discipline Engineer oversees discipline-level engineering
performance of subcontractors, reporting to the CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager.
The main responsibilities of the CONTRACTOR Lead Discipline Engineer are:
- Monitor discipline progress and quality across all subcontractors; escalate issues to the
CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager where required.
- Review discipline deliverables submitted by subcontractors for completeness and
consistency before transmittal to COMPANY.
- Represent CONTRACTOR in COMPANY discipline meetings and design reviews.

3.4.3 CONTRACTOR Interface Manager (VSP)
The CONTRACTOR Interface Manager (VSP) is responsible for managing all engineering
interfaces between VSP and the engineering subcontractors, between different engineering
packages, and between CONTRACTOR and external parties including COMPANY,
Classification Authority (CA), and the Tie-in Host Party. The Interface Manager reports to the
CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager.
The main responsibilities of the CONTRACTOR Interface Manager are:
- Establish, maintain, and update the Interface Data Register (IDR) for all engineering
interfaces across Topsides (PTSC M&C), Jacket and Pipeline (NIPI), Brownfield, and
VSP.
- Identify all engineering interface points between packages at project commencement
and ensure interface data requirements, responsible parties, and delivery dates are
clearly defined and agreed.
- Chair and minute regular interface meetings between PTSC M&C, NIPI, the
Brownfield subcontractor, and VSP; track and follow up on all interface actions to
closure.
- Coordinate the timely issuance and receipt of interface data between engineering
parties, proactively identifying delays or gaps that may impact downstream activities.
- Manage external engineering interfaces with COMPANY, TIE-IN HOST PARTY,
Classification Authority, vendors, and any other third parties, ensuring all interface
obligations are met.
- Maintain a consolidated Interface Action Tracking Register and report open interface
items, risks, and resolution status to the CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager at
weekly engineering coordination meetings.
- Ensure interface data provided to each subcontractor is formally transmitted via
controlled document transmittal and acknowledged as received.
- Coordinate SIMOPS interface requirements between the engineering team and the
Installation/Construction disciplines, ensuring all technical constraints and limitations
are captured in design.

coordination, and production responsibility for all work in his discipline on the project. He is

- Ensuring the technical adequacy and quality of all work produced by his staff;
- Performing engineering on the project as required for his discipline;
- Assigning duty for each member of his discipline, providing necessary technical
guidance; and supervision of their working;
- Proper coordination with other disciplines and on-schedule in-budget completion of all
assigned work;
- Raising any technical issues may cause to design change and schedule throughout the
project execution;
- Other work pertinent to his assigned duties.

3.5 ENGINEERING MOBILIZATION PLAN
In order to meet the requirements of the Project, VSP as CONTRACTOR shall appoint a
dedicated full-time CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager to the Project at the earliest
practicable date. The CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager shall report to the Project
Manager for the successful outcome of the Project.
Immediately upon Contract award, the CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager shall establish
the overall Project Engineering Team, consisting of the VSP Engineering Management Team
(Project Engineer, Lead Discipline Engineer, Document Control Administrator, Interface
Coordinator, and EDMS Administrator), and initiate all activities necessary for the expedient
establishment of the dedicated engineering offices.
Upon the Project Effective Date and start of Detailed Engineering, key personnel shall be
mobilized at an early stage to set up the team, participate in preparation of the Engineering
Execution Plan and associated engineering procedures, and attend the Engineering Kick-Off
Meeting with COMPANY. Following the Kick-Off Meeting, key personnel shall familiarize
themselves with Project documentation, review established priorities, and prepare the detailed
project schedules for implementation of the engineering work.
PTSC M&C shall mobilize its Topsides engineering team in accordance with the Project
schedule and workload, with key discipline leads deployed from project commencement. NIPI
shall mobilize its Jacket and Pipeline engineering team in a similar manner. The Brownfield
engineering subcontractor shall mobilize upon nomination and in accordance with its
confirmed scope and schedule.
3.6 ENGINEERING EXECUTION PROCEDURES
To ensure that the Project accomplishes engineering tasks in a controlled manner, engineering
execution shall utilize project-specific procedures for management and administration, based
on CONTRACTOR's standard procedures adapted for this Project. These procedures shall
cover the following functions:
- Progress reporting, forecasting, and trend control.
- Engineering planning, scheduling, and productivity control.
- Change, cost, and trend control.
- Document control and information management through the Project EDMS.
- Physical progress measurement using the Engineering Master Deliverable Register
(EMDR) and agreed weightage factors.

3.7 COMMUNICATION MANAGEMENT PLAN
3.7.1 Kick-Off Meeting
To finalize the main working points for the Detailed Engineering phase, an overall Engineering
Kick-Off Meeting (KOM) shall be held between COMPANY, VSP, PTSC M&C, and NIPI at
the start of the Project. Parties shall discuss matters regarding the engineering scope of work,
contractual obligations, key interfaces, schedule, and the main working framework. Any
arising issues shall be clarified and resolved amicably by all parties.
In addition to the overall Engineering KOM, separate Discipline KOM meetings shall be
organized between COMPANY's discipline counterparts and CONTRACTOR's Lead
Discipline Engineers (covering Topsides disciplines), as well as the NIPI engineering team
(for Jacket and Pipeline). These discipline KOMs shall confirm scope, deliverable lists, design
basis, schedule, and outstanding FEED items at discipline level.
The Brownfield engineering subcontractor shall hold its own KOM following nomination and
contract award, under the coordination of VSP.
3.7.2 Meetings and Interface Meetings
During Project Execution, weekly engineering coordination meetings shall be organized at the
VSP OCD office to review overall engineering progress, key priorities, interfaces, critical
issues, and required actions across all engineering parties. Representatives from VSP, PTSC
M&C, and NIPI shall attend.
Extraordinary meetings may be organized to discuss urgent matters that arise during
engineering execution. Ad hoc interface meetings and technical review meetings shall be
arranged at the most suitable location and may be conducted via MS Teams where physical
attendance is not practical.
All matters discussed and decisions made during project meetings shall be recorded in Minutes
of Meeting (MOM), distributed to all relevant recipients for review and sign-off, and tracked
for action close-out. MOM duly signed by all participating parties shall be treated as official
Project documents.
Interface meetings between PTSC M&C, NIPI, the Brownfield engineering subcontractor, and
COMPANY shall be organized on a regular basis and tracked through the Interface Data
Register (IDR) in accordance with Section 3.12 of this plan.

PTSC M&C and NIPI shall submit their discipline-level progress data to VSP on a weekly
basis in the agreed format for consolidation into the overall Project Engineering Progress
Report.

submitted by subcontractors, and submitted to COMPANY. Subcontractors are each

A monthly engineering progress report shall also be issued by VSP, providing a more detailed
account of engineering performance.
3.8 ENGINEERING PLANNING AND SCHEDULE MANAGEMENT
A detailed Engineering Schedule shall be developed by VSP in coordination with PTSC M&C
and NIPI, which shall be consistent with the overall EPCI Contract schedule. The Engineering
Schedule shall account for the number and duration of review and approval cycles required by
COMPANY and shall identify all critical path engineering activities.
The detailed Engineering Schedule at Level III shall be mutually agreed between
CONTRACTOR and COMPANY prior to the start of Detailed Engineering. Once agreed, it
shall serve as the baseline for measuring progress and shall only be revised upon written
agreement by both CONTRACTOR and COMPANY through an approved change request.
Individual engineering subcontractors (PTSC M&C and NIPI) shall each maintain their own
engineering sub-schedules, aligned with and consistent with the overall Project Engineering
Schedule maintained by VSP.
Key Engineering Milestones for the Project shall include, but not be limited to:
- FEED Verification and Design Basis freeze (all disciplines).
- Process Simulation Report and Heat and Material Balance (IFR).
- P&IDs (IFR, IFA, AFC) – critical path milestones.
- Equipment Layout (IFR, IFA, AFC).

3.9 DOCUMENT DEVELOPMENT AND CONTROL PROCEDURE
A dedicated Document Control Center (DCC) shall be established by VSP, equipped and
maintained for centralized document and records management utilizing the Project EDMS.
Each engineering office (VSP, PTSC M&C, NIPI) shall have a designated Document
Controller (DC) to perform document and record management to ensure all documentation
produced is gathered, categorized, collated, distributed, and captured in accordance with
Project requirements.
Document numbering shall follow the Project numbering specification as defined in the
governing Project Document Numbering Procedure. All engineering deliverables shall be
identified with a unique document number, revision code, and title.
The revision designation system for engineering deliverables shall follow the sequence: A0
(SDC/IDC), D0/D1/D2 (IFR), E0/E1 (IFA), 0/1/2 (AFC-AFP-IFI), and AB0/AB1 (As-Built).
The review duration for COMPANY and other involved parties shall be ten (10) working days
for IFR or IFA deliverables and five (5) working days for AFC/AFP deliverables. This timeline
shall be reflected in the baseline Engineering Schedule. For urgent cases where earlier return
is required to meet project milestones, the CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager shall make
a formal request to COMPANY.
PTSC M&C shall maintain its own DCC for Topsides deliverables, and NIPI shall maintain
its own DCC for Jacket and Pipeline deliverables. All external submissions to COMPANY
shall be channelled through VSP via official transmittal.

3.12 CHANGE MANAGEMENT PLAN
All changes to the engineering scope, design basis, project specifications, or contractual
requirements shall be managed through a formal Engineering Change Management process.
CONTRACTOR's Change Management Procedure shall be submitted to COMPANY for
approval after the Contract Effective Date.
All proposed changes against the contracted scope of work shall be identified, captured, and
recorded in the Design Change Register. A Design Change Note (DCN) shall be raised for
each proposed change and assessed in terms of technical impact, cost, weight, and schedule
before implementation.
Changes identified by COMPANY shall be reflected in a Change Order or Technical
Instruction (TI) issued to CONTRACTOR. Changes identified by CONTRACTOR shall be
formally raised and submitted to COMPANY for review and authorization before
implementation.
No change shall be implemented without written approval from the appropriate authority. The
impact of each change on Topsides weight shall be specifically evaluated, recognizing weight
growth as a major Project risk due to the limited offshore lifting capacity.
The Design Change Register shall be maintained, updated throughout the Project, and
distributed to all relevant engineering parties for effective Change Control and visibility.
3.13 INTERFACE MANAGEMENT PLAN
Effective interface management is critical to the successful execution of this multi-party
engineering project. VSP as CONTRACTOR shall establish and maintain an Interface
Management Plan to coordinate and control all technical interfaces between VSP, PTSC M&C,
NIPI, the Brownfield engineering subcontractor, COMPANY, vendors, Certify Authority
(CA), and the TIE-IN HOST PARTY.
An Interface Data Register (IDR) shall be established at the start of the Project and maintained
throughout the engineering lifecycle. The IDR shall identify all key engineering interfaces, the
parties responsible for providing and receiving each interface data item, the required delivery
dates, and the current status.

Interface meetings shall be scheduled on a regular basis (at minimum bi-weekly for active

issues. VSP shall chair and minute all inter-party interface meetings. Each engineering

providing required interface data on schedule.
Each engineering party (PTSC M&C and NIPI) shall designate an Interface Coordinator
responsible for managing the IDR within its own scope, ensuring timely issuance of interface
data, and escalating interface issues to VSP and the CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager.
Interface between PTSC M&C Topsides engineering and NIPI Jacket engineering shall be
closely managed for the following key areas:
- Topsides weight and centre of gravity (CoG) data to Jacket design.
- Topsides structural loads and load cases to Jacket structural analysis.
- Deck mating interface, mudmat loading, and connection details.
- Riser and pipeline interfaces at platform base.
- Equipment vendor data affecting Jacket and foundation design.
The Responsibility Matrix and Interface Matrix for the full Project shall be issued as Appendix
C to this document.
3.14 RISK AND OPPORTUNITY MANAGEMENT
Engineering risks and opportunities shall be identified, assessed, and managed throughout the
engineering lifecycle in accordance with CONTRACTOR's Risk Management Procedure.
Engineering risks shall be captured in the Project Risk Register maintained by VSP.
Key engineering risks identified for the Project include: Topsides weight growth exceeding the
heavy lift vessel capacity of approximately 1,000 MT; schedule pressure due to fast-track
execution; incompleteness or discrepancies in FEED deliverables; late vendor data impacting
3D model completion and AFC issuance; interface complexity between Topsides and Jacket
engineering parties; change tie-in point from BK-C to a new subsea tie-in point leading to
extension of 3km pipeline system and late nomination of the Brownfield engineering
subcontractor.
Each engineering party shall proactively identify discipline-specific risks and opportunities
and report them to the VSP Engineering Manager for incorporation into the Project Risk
Register. Risks shall be assessed for likelihood and impact, and mitigation actions shall be
assigned, tracked, and closed.
The Project Risk Register shall be reviewed and updated on a monthly basis and reported to
COMPANY as part of the Monthly Progress Report.

3.15 CONSTRUCTABILITY, OPERABILITY AND MAINTAINABILITY REVIEWS
Constructability, operability, and maintainability reviews shall be conducted at regular
intervals during the Detailed Engineering phase, integrated with the 3D Model Review
sessions at 30%, 60%, and 90% completion. The objective of these reviews is to ensure that
the design facilitates ease of fabrication, construction, installation, hook-up, pre-
commissioning, and commissioning, while also ensuring that operators and maintenance
personnel can work safely and efficiently on the platforms.
Representatives from the CONTRACTOR Construction, Installation, and Commissioning
teams shall participate in these reviews as matrix team members, providing constructability
input from the earliest design stages to avoid unnecessary late rework.
It is essential that fundamental installation philosophies, preferences, and constraints —
including heavy lift vessel limitations, offshore tow/installation procedures, and SIPROD
requirements — are made known to the engineering team at the earliest practicable stage and
incorporated into the design.
Operability and maintainability input from COMPANY's Operations team shall be formally
invited during design reviews. All findings and agreed actions shall be captured in an Action
Tracking Register (ATR) and closed out before AFC issue.
3.16 PROCUREMENT ENGINEERING MANAGEMENT
Procurement Engineering support shall be performed by the engineering teams of PTSC M&C
(for Topsides equipment and materials) and NIPI (for Jacket and Pipeline procurement
packages), with overall coordination and oversight by VSP.
Procurement Support activities performed by Engineering shall include:
- Preparation and issuance of Technical Requisitions (TR), Datasheets (DAS), and
Specifications (SPE) as part of Request for Quotation (RFQ) packages.
- Performance of Technical Bid Clarifications (TBC) and Technical Bid Evaluations
(TBE).
- Preparation and issuance of AFC Technical Requisitions for Purchase Order
attachment.
- Vendor Data Review (VDR) and Vendor Data Incorporation (VDI) into engineering
deliverables.
The schedule for issuance of Procurement Support documents shall be developed in
conjunction with the Project Procurement Manager and incorporated into the Project
Procurement Plan, which serves as the baseline for all procurement activities. The

3.17 TECHNICAL CLARIFICATION MANAGEMENT
3.17.1 Technical Queries
Any technical ambiguities or clarifications required during engineering execution shall be
raised formally through the Technical Query (TQ) process. Preliminary discussion may be
initiated via meeting or email, but shall be formalized through a TQ submission.
All Technical Queries raised by CONTRACTOR during engineering execution shall be
submitted to COMPANY using the official Technical Query form (refer to Appendix G –
Standard Workflows and Templates). Technical Queries shall be treated as official Project
documents.
The procedure for raising a Technical Query is as follows:
- The Lead Discipline Engineer drafts and raises the Technical Query. Each TQ shall be
numbered in accordance with the Project Document Numbering Procedure.
- The TQ shall be submitted to the CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager (VSP) for
review and approval by sign-off (hard copy or soft copy) prior to submission to
COMPANY.
- The approved TQ shall be submitted to COMPANY via DCC transmittal in both PDF
and native format.
- COMPANY shall review and respond to the TQ within a maximum of ten (10) working
days.
- COMPANY's response shall be distributed by the CONTRACTOR Engineering
Manager to the TQ originator and other Lead Discipline Engineers as required.
Document No.: KDP-000-03-PS-G-0001-A0

KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, BLOCK
46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM
PROVISION OF EPCI
KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan
- Both the TQ and COMPANY's response shall be filed by the Document Controller. A
Technical Query Register shall be maintained to log all TQs raised by
CONTRACTOR.
3.17.2 Technical Notes
Technical Notes (TN) shall be issued to present the results of a technical study, defining the
issue investigated, describing the data and methodology used, reporting the conclusions
reached, and presenting recommendations.
Each TN shall be reviewed and approved by the Lead Discipline Engineer and the
CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager before submission to COMPANY. Both the TN and
COMPANY's response shall be filed by the Document Controller.
3.17.3 Deviations, Exceptions and Concessions
Where a Deviation from a project specification, code, or standard is identified as technically
necessary or beneficial, a formal Deviation Request shall be prepared by the originating
discipline and submitted to the CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager for review and
approval. Approved Deviation Requests shall then be submitted to COMPANY for
authorization prior to implementation.
Concessions, which accept non-conforming work or materials after the fact, shall be handled
through the Non-Conformance Report (NCR) process in accordance with the Project Quality
Management procedures.
All approved deviations and concessions shall be formally recorded and tracked in the
Deviation and Concession Register maintained by VSP.
3.18 CORRESPONDENCE MANAGEMENT
Formal letters shall be the official means of communication between CONTRACTOR and
COMPANY. Any decision or confirmation made via formal letter shall be considered official
and must be complied with by both parties.
Email shall be used as an informal but traceable means of communication among project team
members. Email is recommended for routine coordination, follow-up, and confirmation of
verbal discussions. However, email shall not be used to convey decisions on cost, schedule, or
major technical matters — these require formal correspondence.
All official project correspondence shall be routed through the DCC via the EDMS transmittal
system. Response times for formal letters shall be as agreed in the Contract and tracked in the
Correspondence Register maintained by the Document Controller.

3.19 3D MODEL MANAGEMENT
PTSC M&C shall use AVEVA E3D as the primary 3D modelling platform for the KM & DD
WHP Topsides scope. PTSC M&C has established a customized pipe support library and
master catalogue (Cats and Specs database) for AVEVA E3D in parallel with SPMat for
seamless piping component integration.
The 3D Model shall be developed progressively throughout the Detailed Engineering phase
and shall serve as the integrated design environment for all Topsides disciplines including
Process, Mechanical, HVAC, Piping, Electrical, Instrumentation, Structural, and Technical
Safety.
Formal 3D Model Review sessions shall be conducted at 30%, 60%, and 90% completion
stages, with COMPANY and relevant stakeholders in attendance. The purpose of these reviews
is to check the design for clashes, constructability, operability, safety, and compliance with
layout requirements. All review comments and agreed actions shall be captured in the Action
Tracking Register (ATR) and closed out prior to the next model review milestone.
3D model clash detection and management shall be handled via AVEVA Clash Manager. Each
clash recorded shall be assigned to the relevant discipline based on the agreed clash matrix.
All unresolved clashes shall be clearly identified and tracked for resolution.
Data integration between AVEVA E3D and CAESAR II shall be maintained via the AVEVA
Pipe Stress Interface (PSI), eliminating re-modelling of pipes in CAESAR II and ensuring
accurate and efficient pipe stress analysis.
All 3D model databases shall be handed over to COMPANY at project completion in native
format in accordance with the MDR requirements.
3.20 FOLLOW-ON ENGINEERING
Follow-On Engineering (FOE) covers all remaining engineering activities required to support
fabrication, construction, installation, hook-up, commissioning, and final handover of the
Project facilities. FOE shall be executed by PTSC M&C for the Topsides scope and NIPI for
the Jacket and Pipeline scope, under the overall coordination and control of VSP as
CONTRACTOR.
Follow-On Engineering (FOE) shall be executed by PTSC M&C (Topsides) and NIPI (Jacket
and Pipeline) at their respective offices after completion of Detailed Engineering, under the
overall coordination of VSP as CONTRACTOR. Follow-On Engineering covers all remaining
engineering activities required to support fabrication, construction, installation, hook-up,
commissioning, and final handover.

3.21 ENGINEERING CLOSE-OUT
Engineering Close-Out encompasses all activities required to formally conclude the
engineering phase of the Project, confirm that all contractual engineering obligations have
been fulfilled, and ensure that a complete, accurate, and auditable set of engineering records
is delivered to COMPANY. Engineering Close-Out shall be planned and initiated by VSP in
conjunction with PTSC M&C and NIPI during the latter stages of Follow-On Engineering,
and shall be completed prior to the Final Engineering Acceptance.
The Engineering Close-Out process shall cover the following principal activities:
- Confirmation that all engineering deliverables identified in the Engineering Master
Deliverable Register (EMDR) have been completed, issued at the correct approval
status (AFC/AFP/IFI/ASB), and formally accepted by COMPANY. Any outstanding
deliverables shall be identified, scheduled, and resolved to closure.
- Completion and formal issuance of all As-Built engineering deliverables, incorporating
all approved site changes, field modifications, and deviations accepted during
fabrication, construction, installation, hook-up, and commissioning. As-Built drawings
shall reflect the true as-installed condition of all Project facilities.
- Compilation, review, and formal handover of the Manufacturer's Data Reports (MDR)
and Vendor Data Books for all equipment and bulk materials, in accordance with the
MDR Philosophy and the agreed MDR Index. MDR handover to COMPANY shall be
completed in the format specified in the Contract.
- Formal close-out of all open Technical Queries (TQ), Technical Notes (TN), Non-
Conformance Reports (NCR), Deviations, Concessions, Site Technical Queries (STQ),

and HOLD points. No engineering item shall remain open at the time of Final

- Close-out of the Engineering Risk and Opportunity Register: all residual open risks

the Contract.

obligations have been completed and accepted by COMPANY. Demobilization shall
be phased to ensure continuity during the close-out period and shall not commence
until VSP has confirmed completion of all engineering close-out activities with
COMPANY.
- The Engineering Close-Out Schedule, including target completion dates for each close-
out activity and the planned Final Engineering Acceptance date, shall be incorporated
into the overall Project Schedule and tracked as part of the monthly progress reporting.

4 DETAILED DISCIPLINE EXECUTION PLAN
Prior to commencing detailed engineering design activities within their respective scope, PTSC
M&C (for the KM & DD WHP Topsides) and NIPI (for the KM & DD WHP Jackets and
Pipeline) shall each conduct a systematic verification of all COMPANY-supplied data and
design inputs. This verification shall confirm that all required input data — including the FEED
dossier, Basis of Design, project specifications, applicable codes and standards, and any
relevant COMPANY instructions or bulletins — are complete, consistent, and of sufficient
maturity to support the commencement of detailed design. Any missing, ambiguous, or
conflicting input data identified during this verification shall be formally documented as a
HOLD point on the affected deliverable and raised as a Technical Query to VSP, who shall
consolidate and submit to COMPANY for resolution. Detailed design of the affected activity
shall not commence until the required information has been confirmed and the HOLD point
formally cleared.
4.1 GREENFIELD FACILITIES – KM & DD WHPS
4.1.1 Process
Team Organization
The Process design team within PTSC M&C shall be headed by the Lead Process Engineer,
supported by Senior Process Engineers, Process Engineers, and P&ID Designers. The Lead
Process Engineer shall be the focal point for inter-discipline coordination and communication
with COMPANY's Process counterpart. The team shall be organized into sub-groups dedicated
to specific sections of the process and utility systems.
FEED Verification
Process activities shall commence with a design verification of key FEED deliverables
including the Process Basis of Design (BOD) and P&IDs, focusing on identifying deficiencies
that would prevent delivery of a safe and operable facility. A Discipline Kick-Off Meeting
with COMPANY's Process team shall be held within the first week of the Project KOM to
review the deliverables list, design assumptions, and BOD criteria.
Process Simulation and Heat and Material Balance
HYSYS simulation models shall be updated from the FEED models based on the agreed heat
and material balance cases. Heat and Material Balance (HMB) drawings shall be updated after
simulation completion. Process data sheets and specifications for major equipment shall be
prioritized for long lead items to facilitate early procurement.
Document No.: KDP-000-03-PS-G-0001-A0
Page No.: 41 of 57

KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, BLOCK
46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM
PROVISION OF EPCI
KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan
Piping and Instrumentation Diagrams (P&IDs)
P&ID development shall be one of the most intensive process activities during Detailed
Engineering. P&IDs shall be reviewed and updated based on FEED, COMPANY's Tender
Bulletins, and HAZOP findings. It is anticipated that there will be four revision issues: IFR
(after FEED verification and IDC), IFH (Issued for HAZOP – mark-up of IFR), IFA (after
HAZOP findings incorporation), and AFC (after final Vendor data incorporation).
Process Safeguarding
A significant portion of process activity shall focus on overpressure protection, safeguarding,
flaring, and venting design. Safety Analysis Tables (SATs), Shutdown Level Diagrams, and
Process Safeguarding Flow Diagrams developed in FEED shall be further updated. Blowdown
studies shall be performed using HYSYS Blowdown, and flare and vent header modelling shall
be conducted using Aspen Flare System Analyzer based on actual piping isometrics.
Material and Corrosion Engineering
A Material and Corrosion Engineer shall be assigned to the Process team to reconfirm the
FEED Topside Corrosion Analysis and Material Selection Report. CO2 corrosion rate
calculations shall be evaluated using ECE software. Painting, Coating, and Insulation
Specifications shall be developed in accordance with COMPANY requirements and industry
standards applicable to the offshore environment.
Key Process Deliverables
The key deliverables for the Process discipline shall include, but are not limited to: Process
and Utility Basis of Design; Process Simulation Report and HMBs; PFDs and UFDs; P&IDs
(IFR, IFH, IFA, AFC); Process Equipment and Line List; Line Sizing Calculations; Safety
Analysis Tables; Shutdown Level Diagram; Cause and Effect Diagrams; Blowdown and Relief
Study Report; Flare Radiation Report; AIV and FIV Study Reports; System Description
Documents; Corrosion Study and Material Selection Report; Painting/Coating and Insulation
Specifications; and Equipment Datasheets for all mechanical items.
Follow-On Engineering
During Follow-On Engineering, the Process team shall provide all general and design support
required to facilitate fabrication, construction, installation, hook-up, and commissioning. Key
FOE activities for the Process discipline shall include:
- Resolution of Site Technical Queries (STQ) of a process nature; incorporation of any
required changes into P&IDs and process deliverables.
- Review and approval of remaining Vendor data, including approval of PCS/SIS control
narratives and configuration from ICSS Vendor.
Document No.: KDP-000-03-PS-G-0001-A0

4.1.2 Mechanical and HVAC
Organization
A dedicated Mechanical team within PTSC M&C shall consist of a Lead Mechanical Engineer,
Senior Engineers, Engineers, and Senior Designers. The Lead Mechanical Engineer shall serve
as the technical focal point for all Mechanical discipline activities, supported by a dedicated
HVAC sub-team led by a Lead HVAC Engineer. Mechanical discipline scope covers rotating
equipment, pressure vessels and static equipment, package equipment, and material handling
equipment.
FEED Verification and Detailed Engineering
Mechanical activities shall commence with a discipline Kick-Off Meeting with COMPANY's
Mechanical team to align on design approach, scope, deliverables, schedule, and outstanding
FEED items. Upon completion of FEED verification, Mechanical shall prepare the following
primary deliverables: Mechanical Design Basis; Material Handling Philosophy and Report;
Standard Drawings for Pressure Vessels; Mechanical Equipment Datasheets and
Specifications; Technical Requisition Packages (TR); Inspection and Test Plans (ITP); and
Technical Bid Evaluations (TBE). Material Requisitions, Specifications, Mechanical
Datasheets, and ITPs shall be issued for a minimum of three revisions: IFR, IFA, and
AFC/AFP.
HVAC Engineering
HVAC detailed design shall cover all ventilation, air conditioning, and heating systems for the
platform. Vendor selection shall be organized through Technical Requisitions for the HVAC
Equipment Package and Ducting/Piping Bulk Package. Key HVAC deliverables include:
HVAC Design Philosophy; Specification; D&ID; Load Calculations; Datasheets; Equipment
and Duct Layout; MTO; and TBE.
Technical Requisition and Vendor Data Review
TRs for equipment shall be issued progressively based on procurement priority, with long lead
items given first priority. Upon vendor award, Mechanical shall participate in Vendor Kick-

Material Handling Design
The Material Handling Study shall update the FEED Material Handling Philosophy based on
vendor data, covering crane location and coverage, laydown areas, weight of heaviest
maintenance items, and handling routings for major equipment components requiring routine
maintenance.
Key Mechanical Deliverables

and Specifications; Material Handling Study; TR packages and TBEs; ITP; Vendor Data Book;
Weight Control Report inputs; and AFC equipment layout and equipment drawings.
4.1.3 Piping and Layout
Organization
A project-specific Piping and Layout team within PTSC M&C shall be established with a
Piping Lead, Senior Engineers, 3D Administrator, Engineers, Senior Designers, Lead
Designer, Designers, and Draftsmen. Key piping resources shall be mobilized rapidly from
project commencement. The Piping Lead shall be the focal point for all Piping discipline
activities, communication with other disciplines, and the COMPANY's Piping counterpart.
Equipment Layout
Equipment layout development is one of the most critical early Piping activities and shall start
immediately after the FEED Kick-Off Meeting. The layout shall be developed in AVEVA E3D
and shall incorporate all constructability, operability, and maintainability requirements. Layout
shall be issued in a minimum of three revisions: IFR, IFA, and AFC.
Piping Material Engineering
Piping material specifications shall be developed and updated based on the Process and
Corrosion team inputs. A comprehensive Piping Material Class (PMC) system shall be
established covering all service conditions. Line List shall be maintained throughout the design
development capturing all design and operating data for process and utility lines.
Piping Design and 3D Modelling
All piping shall be modelled in AVEVA E3D. Area Design Focal Points shall be designated
for each area/unit, with designers assigned accordingly. Piping General Arrangement (GA)
drawings and isometric drawings shall be generated from the 3D model to the maximum
practicable extent. All piping isometrics shall be issued as AFC for construction.

PROVISION OF EPCI

Pipe Stress Analysis
Pipe stress analysis shall be performed using CAESAR II for all critical piping systems
identified per the stress analysis criteria. The AVEVA Pipe Stress Interface (PSI) shall be used
to transfer pipe geometry from AVEVA E3D to CAESAR II. A final AFC Stress Calculation
Report shall be issued in line with the AFC of construction isometrics. Pipe support loads from
stress analysis shall be transferred to the Structural discipline.
Key Piping Deliverables
Key deliverables include: Piping Design Basis; Piping Material Specifications; Valve and
Fitting Specifications; Line List; Equipment Layout (IFR/IFA/AFC); Piping GA Drawings
(IFR/IFA/AFC); Pipe Support Standards; Piping Isometrics (AFC); Pipe Stress Calculation
Report; MTO; TR packages and TBEs for piping bulk materials and valves.
4.1.4 Instrumentation and Telecom
Organization
The Instrument and Telecom team within PTSC M&C shall consist of a Lead Instrument and
Telecom Engineer, Senior Engineers, Engineers, Senior Designers, and Draftsmen. A
dedicated Sub-Lead Telecom Engineer shall lead the telecommunications sub-team, reporting
to the Lead Instrument and Telecom Engineer. Mobilization shall be phased in accordance
with Project needs and workload.
Objective and Approach
The Instrument and Control discipline shall deliver a well-thought-out, practical, and safe
design meeting COMPANY's requirements in the most efficient manner. The team shall work
closely with COMPANY and CONTRACTOR to achieve early alignment on key system
architectures, seeking to minimize capital cost, operating cost, and weight while adhering to
Project specifications and regulatory requirements.
Instrumentation Detail Engineering Design
Once the overall Instrument design approach has been agreed and required inter-discipline
inputs are available, the Instrument team shall prepare the following deliverables: Instrument
Design Basis; Control and Shutdown Philosophy; Metering Philosophy; Alarm Management
Philosophy; Fiscal Metering Specification; Control Narrative; F&G Cause and Effect
Diagrams; Field Instruments and Valves Datasheets and Specifications; TR packages; TBEs;
Instrument Schedule; I/O Schedule (PCS/SIS/FGS); Trip and Alarm Settings; Ex
Register/Schedule List; F&G Devices Datasheets; Instrument Room Layout; Cable
Ladder/Tray Layout Drawings; Fire and Gas Layout Drawings; Instrument Layout Drawings;
Cable Schedule; Loop Schematics; Junction Box/Wiring Drawings; and Bulk MTO.

4.1.6 Structural – Topsides
Scope and Organization
The Structural Topsides team within PTSC M&C shall be responsible for the detailed structural
engineering of the KM & DD WHP Topsides and Substructures (excluding the Jacket, which
is under NIPI's scope). The team shall consist of a Lead Structural Engineer, Senior Structural
Engineers, Structural Design Engineers, a Weight Control Engineer, a Building Architect, a
Lead Designer, 3D model operators, and 2D draftsmen.
Structural Engineering Execution
The structural engineering execution shall systematically progress through the following
stages: (1) Primary structure definition and MTO — including FEED verification, MDR
establishment, constructability review, fire and blast load definition, primary steel MTO for
procurement, and weight budget setup; (2) Secondary steel development — including primary
structure finalization, secondary steel definition with vendor data, equipment foundation
design, pipe support design, and weight control updates; (3) Tertiary steel finalization —
including final secondary steel and tertiary items, AFC drawings production and 90% model
review response.
Weight Control
Weight control is a critical discipline activity on this Project, given the offshore lifting capacity
limitation of the designated Heavy Lift Vessel (~1,000 MT). A dedicated Weight Control
Engineer shall be assigned to compile and update the Weight Control Report on a monthly
basis, collecting weight and Centre of Gravity (CoG) data from all disciplines. All discipline
Lead Engineers are responsible for providing accurate and timely weight data in the agreed
format, segregated by deck level. Weight growth shall be monitored against established
budgets and limits throughout the engineering lifecycle.
Key Structural Topsides Deliverables
Key deliverables include: Structural Design Basis; Structural Analysis Calculations; Primary
and Secondary Steel Drawings (AFC); Structural MTO and Bills of Material; Fabrication
Drawings and Shop Drawings; Equipment Foundation Drawings; Special Pipe Support
Drawings; Architectural Drawings; Weight Control Reports; and 3D Model (AVEVA E3D).

4.1.7 Structural – Jacket and Substructure
Organization
To perform Jacket design, NIPI will assign Structure team, Naval team and Anti-Corrosion
team as the organization chart. The team shall consist of Lead Engineers, Senior Engineers,
Engineers, Lead Designer, and 2D draftsmen.
FEED verification
After receiving input data, 3 disciplines shall perform FEED verification by:
- Checking FEED analysis, reports and updating modelling as latest input to verify
simulation and calculation;
- Checking PO and FEED MTO to verify necessary quantity.
All findings with potential impact on cost and schedule shall be put in the FEED verification
register.
Jacket Engineering Execution
In order to meet procurement plan, MTOs, purchase requisition, specification for primary &
secondary steel structure and Jacket anode shall be put in submission priority.
In parallel, following activities shall be performed and submitted later:
- Jacket for in-service analyses (i.e. in-place, jacket fatigue, jacket foundation) and pre-
service analysis (i.e. loadout, transportation, jacket launching, jacket floatation and
upending, jacket On-bottom stability);
- Jacket miscellaneous analysis and detailed secondary structures;
- Boat Landing Design;
- Transportation, upending and lifting analysis;
- MTOs, purchase requisition, specification for miscellaneous;
- Primary and secondary structure drawings;
- Detailed drawings;
- Transportation, upending and lifting sequences;
- Monitoring the weight growth through weight control engineer;
- Performing miscellaneous design and drafting for non vendor-item access platforms,
monorail beams (if required)...;
- Cathodic protection report, Anode installation and arrangement drawings for pipelines
and Jackets;
- Developing and updating 3D model, be representative for NIPI in 3d Model
workshops;
- VDR & VDI;

4.1.8 Technical Safety
Organization and Objective
The Technical Safety team within PTSC M&C shall consist of a Lead Technical Safety
Engineer, Senior Engineers, Engineers, and Designers. The Lead Technical Safety Engineer
shall be the focal point for all Safety discipline activities, coordinating with COMPANY and
other disciplines. The main objective of Technical Safety Engineering is to ensure that Safety
Engineering requirements are complied with in the Detailed Engineering phase, and that all
safety studies and loss prevention designs are properly executed.
Formal Safety Assessment Studies
The Technical Safety team shall manage specialist safety consultants (approved by
COMPANY) to undertake the following Formal Safety Assessment studies to ensure risks are
reduced to As Low As Reasonably Practicable (ALARP):
- HAZID and HAZOP workshops (facilitated by experienced third-party).
- SIMOPS review.
- SIL Classification and Verification.
- 3D Explosion Risk Analysis.
- Fire Risk Analysis (FRA).
- Quantitative Risk Assessment (QRA).
- Escape, Evacuation and Rescue Analysis (EERA).
- Emergency System Survivability Analysis (ESSA).
- Dropped Object Study (DOS).
- Noise Study.
- 3D Fire and Gas Mapping Study.
- ALARP workshop and Safety Critical Equipment and Performance Standards
(SCE&PS).
- HSE Safety Case.

register.

system shall be put in submission priority.

5 ENGINEERING QUALITY ASSURANCE AND DESIGN CONTROL
5.1 ENGINEERING QUALITY ASSURANCE PLAN
This Engineering Quality Assurance Plan (EQAP) defines the controls and provisions to be
implemented throughout the duration of the Project to ensure that all key engineering
deliverables are completed on schedule without compromise of quality.
The provisions of this EQAP are intended to ensure that:
- Adequate controls are exercised during the execution of engineering in accordance with
the Contract.
- The workmanship, equipment, materials, and services delivered meet all legal and
contractual requirements including the quality expected by COMPANY.
- Auditable records and documentation are produced and made available to COMPANY
to demonstrate compliance with contractual requirements.
- Mistakes and defects during engineering execution are prevented and problems when
delivering documents or services to COMPANY are avoided.
- All engineering parties (VSP, PTSC M&C, NIPI, Brownfield subcontractor)
implement the Project procedures and schedules as planned.
5.1.1 Engineering Design Control
The Lead Engineer of each discipline shall prepare a list of deliverables under his/her
responsibility, with reference to the contractual Scope of Work. These lists shall be
consolidated into the Engineering Master Deliverable Register (EMDR), which shall identify
target and actual completion dates, physical progress percentages, document numbers, titles,
document approval class, and revision status. The EMDR shall be updated and maintained by
the Project Engineer throughout the Project.
Document numbering for all Project deliverables shall follow the Project Document
Numbering Procedure. Revision numbering and designation shall comply with the following
scheme: A0 (SDC/IDC); D0/D1/D2 (Issued for Review – IFR); E0/E1 (Issued for Approval –
IFA); 0/1/2 (Approved for Construction/Purchase/Information – AFC/AFP/IFI); and
AB1/AB2 (As-Built – ASB).
Document changes shall be identified in Word files by a vertical blue revision line in the right
margin. For AutoCAD drawings, changes shall be indicated by a revision cloud and a triangle
containing the revision code. For Excel/datasheet files, changes shall be highlighted in blue
italic font.

KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, BLOCK
46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM
PROVISION OF EPCI
KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan
5.2 ENGINEERING INPUT CONTROL
Prior to commencing any design and engineering activity, Lead Engineers shall confirm the
adequacy of the design input information available in the Contract documents, including the
Project Basis of Design, FEED dossier, and referenced project standards, codes, and
specifications.
Each discipline shall have access to all applicable FEED Design Documents and Project
Standards relevant to its scope of work through the EDMS and Project Engineering Server.
Lead Engineers shall ensure that design activities are performed in accordance with established
Project standards, procedures, and codes of practice within the contracted scope of work.
Technical assumptions and outstanding FEED items that cannot be confirmed at the start of
Detailed Engineering shall be clearly documented, registered, and tracked. HOLD points shall
be clearly identified on affected deliverables until the required information is available and
confirmed.
5.3 ENGINEERING OUTPUT CONTROL
Engineering deliverables (calculations, drawings, specifications, procedures, analyses, etc.)
shall be documented in a complete and unambiguous form compatible with and traceable to
design inputs. All deliverables shall be registered in the EMDR and the design output shall
reference the relevant acceptance criteria in accordance with COMPANY's requirements.
Characteristics of the design that are crucial to the safe and proper function of the end products
shall be identified in design output documentation, particularly for fabrication or construction
purposes.
Lead Engineers are responsible for ensuring that engineering output documentation is
reviewed carefully for adequacy before submission to COMPANY. The CONTRACTOR
Engineering Manager or his designee shall approve all engineering deliverables before they
are submitted to COMPANY or CA for external review. Notwithstanding CONTRACTOR's
approval, the technical adequacy, accuracy, and completeness of each engineering deliverable
shall remain the direct accountability of the originating subcontractor's Lead Engineer and
Engineering Manager, who shall be responsible for the correctness of the technical content
within their assigned scope.
5.4 DESIGN CHECKING AND VERIFICATION
Design checking shall follow a structured sequence of increasing rigor before external
submission. The standard checking sequence shall be:
- Self Check by the originator.
Document No.: KDP-000-03-PS-G-0001-A0
Page No.: 53 of 57

KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, BLOCK
46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM
PROVISION OF EPCI
KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan
- Single Discipline Check (SDC) by a qualified checker within the discipline.
- Inter-Discipline Check (IDC) by all relevant disciplines.
- External Review and Approval (IFR / IFA / AFC / IFI) by COMPANY and other
project parties.
5.4.1 Self Check
Before issuing any revision of a document, the Originator shall perform a self-check using the
applicable check sheet. The self-check shall verify: completeness of the document; correct
format, document number, and revision coding; compliance with design criteria and input data;
compliance with applicable regulations and standards; and proper identification of any HOLD
information.
After completing the self-check, the Originator shall sign the check sheet and save it on the
Project discipline server before progressing to the SDC stage.
5.4.2 Single Discipline Check (SDC)
Following self-checking, a Single Discipline Check shall be conducted by a suitably qualified
and experienced checker within the discipline, appointed by the Lead Discipline Engineer. The
SDC shall confirm adequacy of technical content, accuracy of technical inputs, proper
identification of reference documents, compliance with project standards, identification of
HOLD items, and that COMPANY and regulatory requirements have been addressed.
SDC shall be conducted through the EDMS or the Project Discipline Server. The Originator
shall incorporate all SDC comments and issue the document for IDC. A Comment Response
Sheet (CRS) shall be used to track comment disposition.
5.4.3 Inter-Discipline Check (IDC)
After SDC, engineering deliverables shall be subjected to a multi-discipline Inter-Discipline
Check (IDC) to ensure that all relevant disciplines can review design produced by another
discipline and check the adequacy of interfaces. The full list of documents issued for IDC shall
be presented in the IDC Review Matrix.
Time allocated for IDC shall generally be a maximum of five (5) working days from the date
of issue. The Originator shall consolidate all IDC comments, generate a CRS, and incorporate
relevant comments before proceeding to external submission.

KM-WHP & DD-WHP Engineering Execution and Quality Assurance Plan
5.4.4 Project Approval for External Review and Issue Status Control (IFR / IFA / AFC / IFI)
Before a document is submitted to COMPANY for Review or Approval, it shall be approved
by the Lead Discipline Engineer and the CONTRACTOR Engineering Manager. The approved
document, together with the internal CRS for IDC comments, shall be submitted via DCC
transmittal as IFR, IFA, AFC, or IFI as applicable.
COMPANY shall review and return comments within ten (10) working days for IFR and IFA,
and five (5) working days for AFC. Comments not incorporated by CONTRACTOR shall be
discussed and agreed with COMPANY. A Comment Response Sheet shall be issued by
CONTRACTOR in response to all COMPANY comments.
5.5 DESIGN REVIEW WORKSHOPS
During Project execution, safety and design review workshops shall be conducted to review
all aspects of the work including safety, operability, maintainability, constructability,
accessibility, and material handling. The primary workshops planned are HAZID, HAZOP,
SIL Classification, and three 3D Model Reviews at 30%, 60%, and 90% completion. The dates
for these workshops shall be included in the Engineering Key Milestones table in Appendix E.
In addition to the primary planned workshops, ad hoc design review workshops shall be
conducted internally or with COMPANY attendance when deemed necessary during the
course of the Project.
5.6 MANAGEMENT OF REVIEW COMMENTS AND CLOSE-OUT
A Comment Response Sheet (CRS) shall be generated by the Originator upon receipt of
comments from other disciplines, from COMPANY, or from any external reviewer. The CRS
shall clearly indicate which comments have been incorporated and which have not, with
justified reasons for non-incorporation.
Comments not incorporated shall be discussed and agreed with the Reviewer and/or
COMPANY Approver to avoid unnecessary re-cycling. All comment dispositions shall be
recorded in the CRS and filed in the EDMS with the document.
CONTRACTOR shall ensure that all COMPANY comments are responded to in a timely
manner. Any disputed comments shall be escalated to the CONTRACTOR Engineering
Manager and COMPANY Engineering Manager for resolution.

5.7 QUALITY MANAGEMENT AND AUDIT PLAN
Quality records necessary to provide audit trail and demonstrate conformance to Contract
requirements shall be maintained throughout the Project. These records include: Contract
documents and change notices; all technical deliverables; correspondence and Minutes of
Meetings; progress reports; the EMDR; planning schedules; project procedures; design review
reports; and audit reports.
Engineering quality shall be ensured through the following mechanisms: (1) Design checking
by engineering teams as described in Sections 6.4.1 to 6.4.4 above; (2) Internal
CONTRACTOR Audit by CONTRACTOR QAQC (with COMPANY as observer).
Engineering QA Audits shall be led by the CONTRACTOR Lead Auditor in accordance with
the Project Audit Schedule. A minimum of one week advance notice together with the audit
charter shall be given to all concerned parties, including COMPANY, prior to the audit.
COMPANY may request to observe any quality audit conducted by VSP or its subcontractors
upon reasonable advance notice. Non-conformances identified shall be solely the
responsibility of the subcontractor within whose scope they arise. Each subcontractor shall
prepare and submit its corrective action plan to VSP within 14 working days for onward
transmittal to COMPANY.
5.8 ENGINEERING KPI
Engineering Quality KPIs for this Project shall be defined, owned, and reported by each
responsible party for its own scope. Each party shall monitor its own KPIs, implement
corrective actions within its scope, and report KPI performance directly to VSP and
COMPANY. VSP shall consolidate and report overall KPI status to COMPANY in the
Monthly Progress Report. Each subcontractor is directly accountable to VSP and COMPANY
for its own KPI performance and corrective actions.
Document No.: KDP-000-03-PS-G-0001-A0
Page No.: 56 of 57
